<p><b>Sir Michael Philip Jagger</b> (born 26 July 1943),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whoswho_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> known professionally as <b>Mick Jagger</b>, is an English musician, singer-songwriter and one time actor, best known as the lead vocalist and a founder member of <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">the Rolling Stones</a>.</p>
<p>Jagger's career has spanned over 50 years, and he has been described as "one of the most popular and influential frontmen in the history of rock &amp; roll".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> His distinctive voice and performance, along with <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a>' guitar style, have been the trademark of the Rolling Stones throughout the career of the band. Jagger gained press notoriety for his admitted drug use and romantic involvements, and was often portrayed as a <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">countercultural</a> figure. In the late 1960s Jagger began acting in films (starting with <i><a href="/wiki/Performance_(film)" title="Performance (film)">Performance</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly_(1970_film)" title="Ned Kelly (1970 film)">Ned Kelly</a></i>), to mixed reception. In 1985, Jagger released his first <a href="/wiki/Solo_album" title="Solo album">solo album</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/She%27s_the_Boss" title="She's the Boss">She's the Boss</a></i>. In early 2009, he joined the electric <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> <a href="/wiki/SuperHeavy" title="SuperHeavy">SuperHeavy</a>.</p>
<p>In 1989 Jagger was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>, and in 2004 into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> with the Rolling Stones. In 2003 he was <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> for his services to music.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1943.E2.80.9361:_early_years">1943–61: early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 1943–61: early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="noprint portal tright" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em">
<table style="background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;max-width:175px">
<tr style="vertical-align:middle">
<td style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stones_members_montage.JPG"><img alt="Portal icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="755" data-file-width="822" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ee/Stones_members_montage.JPG/31px-Stones_members_montage.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ee/Stones_members_montage.JPG/46px-Stones_members_montage.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ee/Stones_members_montage.JPG/61px-Stones_members_montage.JPG 2x" width="31"/></a></td>
<td style="padding:0 0.2em;vertical-align:middle;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Portal:The_Rolling_Stones" title="Portal:The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones portal</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>Jagger was born into a middle-class family in <a href="/wiki/Dartford" title="Dartford">Dartford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> His father, Basil Fanshawe "Joe" Jagger (13 April 1913 – 11 November 2006), and grandfather, David Ernest Jagger, were both teachers. His mother, Eva Ensley Mary (née Scutts; 6 April 1913 – 18 May 2000), born in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Australia, of English descent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> was a hairdresser<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and an active member of the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>. Jagger's younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jagger" title="Chris Jagger">Chris</a> (born 19 December 1947) is also a musician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The two have performed together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although brought up to follow his father's career path, Jagger "was always a singer" as he stated in <i>According to the Rolling Stones</i>. "I always sang as a child. I was one of those kids who just <i>liked</i> to sing. Some kids sing in choirs; others like to show off in front of the mirror. I was in the church choir and I also loved listening to singers on the radio--the BBC or <a href="/wiki/Radio_Luxembourg_(English)" title="Radio Luxembourg (English)">Radio Luxembourg</a>--or watching them on TV and in the movies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-accordingto2003p13_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-accordingto2003p13-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From September 1950, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a> and Jagger were classmates at Wentworth Primary School, <a href="/wiki/Dartford" title="Dartford">Dartford</a>, Kent. In 1954, Jagger passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a>, and went to <a href="/wiki/Dartford_Grammar_School" title="Dartford Grammar School">Dartford Grammar School</a>, which now has <a href="/wiki/The_Mick_Jagger_Centre" title="The Mick Jagger Centre">the Mick Jagger Centre</a> installed within the school's site, named for its most famous alumnus. Jagger and Richards lost contact with each other when they went to different schools, but after a chance encounter in July 1960, resumed their friendship and discovered their shared love of <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a>, which for Jagger had begun with <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">Little Richard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitep119-120_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-whitep119-120-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger left school in 1961 after obtaining 7 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O-levels" title="O-levels">O-levels</a> and 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-levels" title="A-levels">A-levels</a>. Jagger and Richards moved into a flat in Edith Grove in <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_London" title="Chelsea, London">Chelsea, London</a> with a guitarist they had encountered named <a href="/wiki/Brian_Jones" title="Brian Jones">Brian Jones</a>. While Richards and Jones planned to start their own rhythm and blues group, Jagger continued his business courses at the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and had seriously considered becoming either a journalist or a politician, comparing the latter to a pop star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1962.E2.80.93present:_the_Rolling_Stones">1962–present: the Rolling Stones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1962–present: the Rolling Stones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="785" data-file-width="800" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg/220px-Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg/330px-Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg/440px-Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_1965.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
21-year-old Mick Jagger before a Rolling Stones concert at Georgia Southern College, 4 May 1965</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In their earliest days; the members played for no money in the interval of <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Korner" title="Alexis Korner">Alexis Korner</a>'s gigs at a basement club opposite <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Broadway_station" title="Ealing Broadway station">Ealing Broadway</a> tube station (subsequently called "Ferry's" club). At the time, the group had very little equipment and needed to borrow Alexis' gear to play. This was before <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Loog_Oldham" title="Andrew Loog Oldham">Andrew Loog Oldham</a> became their manager. The group's first appearance under the name the Rollin' Stones (after one of their favourite <a href="/wiki/Muddy_Waters" title="Muddy Waters">Muddy Waters</a> tunes) was at the <a href="/wiki/Marquee_Club" title="Marquee Club">Marquee Club</a> in London, a jazz club, on 12 July 1962. They would later change their name to "the Rolling Stones" as it seemed more formal. Victor Bockris states that the band members included Mick Jagger, Keith Richards, Brian Jones, Ian Stewart on piano, Dick Taylor on bass and Tony Chapman on drums. However, Richards states in <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(book)" title="Life (book)">Life</a></i>, "The drummer that night was Mick Avory--not Tony Chapman, as history has mysteriously handed it down..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Avory himself has categorically denied "on many occasions"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> that he played with the Rollin' Stones that night. In fact he only rehearsed twice with them in the Bricklayers Arms pub, before they became known as the Rollin' Stones. Some time later, the band went on their first tour in the United Kingdom; this was known as the "training ground" tour because it was a new experience for all of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The line-up did not at that time include drummer <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Watts" title="Charlie Watts">Charlie Watts</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Bill_Wyman" title="Bill Wyman">Bill Wyman</a>. By 1963, they were finding their stride as well as popularity. By 1964, two unscientific opinion polls rated them as Britain's most popular group, outranking even <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By autumn 1963, Jagger had left the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a> in favour of his promising musical career with the Rolling Stones. The group continued to mine the works of American rhythm and blues artists such as <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bo_Diddley" title="Bo Diddley">Bo Diddley</a>, but with the strong encouragement of Andrew Loog Oldham, Jagger and Richards soon began to write their own songs. This <a href="/wiki/Jagger/Richards" title="Jagger/Richards">core songwriting partnership</a> would flourish in time; one of their early compositions, "<a href="/wiki/As_Tears_Go_By_(song)" title="As Tears Go By (song)">As Tears Go By</a>", was a song written for <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Faithfull" title="Marianne Faithfull">Marianne Faithfull</a>, a young singer Loog Oldham was promoting at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-accordingtop84_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-accordingtop84-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> For the Rolling Stones, the duo would write "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Last_Time_(song)" title="The Last Time (song)">The Last Time</a>", the group's third No. 1 single in the UK (their first two UK No. 1 hits had been <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cover_versions" title="Cover versions">cover versions</a>) based on <i>This May Be the Last Time</i>, a traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negro_spiritual" title="Negro spiritual">Negro spiritual</a> song recorded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staple_Singers" title="Staple Singers">Staple Singers</a> in 1955. Another fruit of this collaboration was their first international hit, "<a href="/wiki/(I_Can%27t_Get_No)_Satisfaction" title="(I Can't Get No) Satisfaction">(I Can't Get No) Satisfaction</a>". It also established the Rolling Stones' image as defiant troublemakers in contrast to the Beatles' "lovable moptop" image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger told <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Schiff" title="Stephen Schiff">Stephen Schiff</a> in a 1992 <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> profile: "I wasn't trying to be rebellious in those days; I was just being me. I wasn't trying to push the edge of anything. I'm being me and ordinary, the guy from suburbia who sings in this band, but someone older might have thought it was just the most awful racket, the most terrible thing, and where are we going if this is music?... But all those songs we sang were pretty tame, really. People didn't think they were, but I thought they were tame."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The group released several successful albums including <i><a href="/wiki/December%27s_Children_(And_Everybody%27s)" title="December's Children (And Everybody's)">December's Children (And Everybody's)</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aftermath_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Aftermath (The Rolling Stones album)">Aftermath</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Between_the_Buttons" title="Between the Buttons">Between the Buttons</a></i>, but in their personal lives and behaviour were brought into question. In 1967, Jagger and Richards were arrested on drug charges and were given unusually harsh sentences: Jagger was sentenced to three months' imprisonment for possession of four over-the-counter pep pills he had purchased in Italy. On appeal, Richards' sentence was overturned and Jagger's was amended to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conditional_discharge" title="Conditional discharge">conditional discharge</a> (he ended up spending one night inside London's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brixton_Prison" title="Brixton Prison">Brixton Prison</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> after <a href="/wiki/Who_breaks_a_butterfly_upon_a_wheel%3F#Modern_use" title="Who breaks a butterfly upon a wheel?">an article</a> appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">the Times</a></i>, written by its traditionally conservative editor <a href="/wiki/William_Rees-Mogg" title="William Rees-Mogg">William Rees-Mogg</a>, but the Rolling Stones continued to face legal battles for the next decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="780" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg/220px-Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg/330px-Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg/440px-Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_in_red.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mick Jagger on stage in July 1972, New York</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1970, Jagger bought <a href="/wiki/Stargroves" title="Stargroves">Stargroves</a>, a manor house and estate in <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>. The Rolling Stones and several other bands recorded there using a <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_Mobile_Studio" title="Rolling Stones Mobile Studio">mobile studio</a>.</p>
<p>After Jones's death and their move in 1971 to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_of_France" title="South of France">south of France</a> as tax exiles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger and the rest of the band changed their look and style as the 1970s progressed. He also learned to play guitar and contributed guitar parts for certain songs on <i><a href="/wiki/Sticky_Fingers" title="Sticky Fingers">Sticky Fingers</a></i> (1971) and all subsequent albums (with the exception of <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Work_(The_Rolling_Stones_album)" title="Dirty Work (The Rolling Stones album)">Dirty Work</a></i> in 1986). For the Rolling Stones' highly publicised 1972 American tour, Jagger wore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glam-rock" title="Glam-rock">glam-rock</a> clothing and glittery makeup on stage. Later in the decade, they ventured into genres like <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> with the album <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Girls" title="Some Girls">Some Girls</a></i> (1978). Their interest in the blues, however, had been made manifest in the 1972 album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exile_on_Main_St" title="Exile on Main St">Exile on Main St</a></i>. His emotional singing on the gospel-influenced "<a href="/wiki/Let_It_Loose_(song)" title="Let It Loose (song)">Let It Loose</a>", one of the album's tracks, has been described by music critic Russell Hall as having been Jagger's finest ever vocal achievement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the band's acrimonious split with their second manager, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Klein" title="Allen Klein">Allen Klein</a>, in 1971, Jagger took control of their business affairs after speaking with an up-and-coming front man, JB Silver, and has managed them ever since in collaboration with his friend and colleague, Rupert Löwenstein. <a href="/wiki/Mick_Taylor" title="Mick Taylor">Mick Taylor</a>, Brian Jones's replacement, left the band in December 1974 and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Faces_(band)" title="Faces (band)">Faces</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Wood" title="Ronnie Wood">Ronnie Wood</a> in 1975, who also operated as a mediator within the group, and between Jagger and Richards in particular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2225" data-file-width="3069" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Rolling_Stones_09.jpg/220px-Rolling_Stones_09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Rolling_Stones_09.jpg/330px-Rolling_Stones_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Rolling_Stones_09.jpg/440px-Rolling_Stones_09.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger in Torino, Italy in 1982</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While continuing to tour and release albums with the Rolling Stones, Jagger began a solo career. In 1985, he released his first solo album <i><a href="/wiki/She%27s_the_Boss" title="She's the Boss">She's the Boss</a></i> produced by <a href="/wiki/Nile_Rodgers" title="Nile Rodgers">Nile Rodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Laswell" title="Bill Laswell">Bill Laswell</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Herbie_Hancock" title="Herbie Hancock">Herbie Hancock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Hammer" title="Jan Hammer">Jan Hammer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Compass_Point_All_Stars" title="Compass Point All Stars">Compass Point All Stars</a>. It sold fairly well, and the single "Just Another Night" was a Top Ten hit. During this period, he collaborated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Jacksons" title="The Jacksons">the Jacksons</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/State_of_Shock_(song)" title="State of Shock (song)">State of Shock</a>", sharing lead vocals with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>.</p>
<p>For his own personal contributions in the 1985 <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> multi-venue charity concert, he performed at <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JFK_Stadium" title="JFK Stadium">JFK Stadium</a>; he did a duet with <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> of "It's Only Rock and Roll", and the performance was highlighted by Jagger tearing away Turner's skirt. He also did a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Dancing_in_the_Street" title="Dancing in the Street">Dancing in the Street</a>" with <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, who himself appeared at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>. The video was shown simultaneously on the screens of both Wembley and JFK Stadiums. The song reached number one in the UK the same year. In 1987, he released his second solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Primitive_Cool" title="Primitive Cool">Primitive Cool</a></i>. While it failed to match the commercial success of his debut, it was critically well received. In 1988, he produced the songs "Glamour Boys" and "Which Way to America" on <a href="/wiki/Living_Colour" title="Living Colour">Living Colour</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Vivid_(Living_Colour_album)" title="Vivid (Living Colour album)">Vivid</a></i>. 15–28 March, he had a solo concert tour in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Wandering_Spirit_(album)" title="Wandering Spirit (album)">Wandering Spirit</a></i> was the third solo album by Jagger and was released in 1993. It would be his only solo album release of the 1990s. Jagger aimed to re-introduce himself as a solo artist in a musical climate vastly changed from that of his first two albums, <i>She's the Boss</i> and <i>Primitive Cool</i>.</p>
<p>Following the successful comeback of the Rolling Stones' <i><a href="/wiki/Steel_Wheels" title="Steel Wheels">Steel Wheels</a></i> (1989), which saw the end of Jagger and Richards' well-publicised feud, after acquiring <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a> as co-producer in January 1992 Jagger began recording the album in Los Angeles over seven months until September 1992, recording simultaneously as Richards was making <i><a href="/wiki/Main_Offender" title="Main Offender">Main Offender</a></i>.</p>
<p>Jagger would keep the celebrity guests to a minimum on <i>Wandering Spirit</i>, only having <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz" title="Lenny Kravitz">Lenny Kravitz</a> as a vocalist on his cover of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Withers" title="Bill Withers">Bill Withers</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Use_Me_(Bill_Withers_song)" title="Use Me (Bill Withers song)">Use Me</a>" and bassist <a href="/wiki/Flea_(musician)" title="Flea (musician)">Flea</a> from <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers" title="Red Hot Chili Peppers">Red Hot Chili Peppers</a> on three tracks. Following the end of the Rolling Stones' Sony Music contract and their signing to <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin Records</a>, Jagger signed with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a> (which had signed the Stones in the 1970s) to distribute what would be his only album with the label. Released in February 1993, <i>Wandering Spirit</i> was commercially successful, reaching No.12 in the UK and No.11 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="1960" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG/170px-Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG/255px-Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG/340px-Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jagger_live_Italy_2003.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger live at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, Italy in 2003</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, Jagger released <i><a href="/wiki/Goddess_in_the_Doorway" title="Goddess in the Doorway">Goddess in the Doorway</a></i> spawning the hit single "Visions of Paradise". In the same year, he also joined Keith Richards in <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_New_York_City" title="The Concert for New York City">the Concert for New York City</a>, a charity concert in response to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">11 September attacks</a>, to sing "<a href="/wiki/Salt_of_the_Earth_(song)" title="Salt of the Earth (song)">Salt of the Earth</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Miss_You_(The_Rolling_Stones_song)" title="Miss You (The Rolling Stones song)">Miss You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He celebrated the Rolling Stones' 40th anniversary by touring with them on the year-long <a href="/wiki/Licks_Tour" title="Licks Tour">Licks Tour</a> in support of their career retrospective <i><a href="/wiki/Forty_Licks" title="Forty Licks">Forty Licks</a></i> double album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, the Rolling Stones made US$437 million on their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang_Tour" title="A Bigger Bang Tour">A Bigger Bang Tour</a>, which got them into the current edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> for the most lucrative music tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger has refused to say when the band will retire, stating in 2007: "I'm sure the Rolling Stones will do more things and more records and more tours. We've got no plans to stop any of that really."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2009, Jagger and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> performed "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_Shelter" title="Gimme Shelter">Gimme Shelter</a>" (with <a href="/wiki/Fergie_(singer)" title="Fergie (singer)">Fergie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>) and "<a href="/wiki/Stuck_in_a_Moment_You_Can%27t_Get_Out_Of" title="Stuck in a Moment You Can't Get Out Of">Stuck in a Moment You Can't Get Out Of</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame#25th_anniversary_concert" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">25th Anniversary Rock &amp; Roll Hall of Fame Concert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 20 May 2011, Jagger announced the formation of a new <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a>, <a href="/wiki/SuperHeavy" title="SuperHeavy">SuperHeavy</a>, which includes <a href="/wiki/David_A._Stewart" title="David A. Stewart">Dave Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joss_Stone" title="Joss Stone">Joss Stone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damian_Marley" title="Damian Marley">Damian Marley</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.R._Rahman" title="A.R. Rahman">A.R. Rahman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger has featured on <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>'s 2011 single "<a href="/wiki/T.H.E._(The_Hardest_Ever)" title="T.H.E. (The Hardest Ever)">T.H.E. (The Hardest Ever)</a>". It was officially released to iTunes on 4 February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_26.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2165" data-file-width="2896" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rolling_Stones_26.jpg/220px-Rolling_Stones_26.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rolling_Stones_26.jpg/330px-Rolling_Stones_26.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Rolling_Stones_26.jpg/440px-Rolling_Stones_26.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rolling_Stones_26.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger performing with the Stones at <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park, London</a> in July 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 21 February 2012, Mick Jagger, <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> along with a blues ensemble performed at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> concert series before President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>. When Jagger held out a mic to him, Obama sang twice the line "Come on, baby don't you want to go" of the blues cover '<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Home_Chicago" title="Sweet Home Chicago">Sweet Home Chicago</a>', the blues anthem of Obama's home town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger hosted the season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on 19 and 20 May 2012, doing several comic skits and playing some of the Rolling Stones' hits with Arcade Fire, Foo Fighters, and Jeff Beck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger performed in <a href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief" title="12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief">12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief</a> with the Rolling Stones on 12 December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The Stones finally played the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glastonbury_festival" title="Glastonbury festival">Glastonbury festival</a> in 2013, headlining on Saturday 29 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> This was followed by two concerts in London's <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> as part of their 50th anniversary celebrations, their first in the Park since their famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stones_in_the_Park" title="Stones in the Park">1969 performance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, Mick Jagger teamed up with his brother <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jagger" title="Chris Jagger">Chris Jagger</a> for two new duets to mark the 40th anniversary of Chris' debut album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendship_with_Keith_Richards">Friendship with Keith Richards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Friendship with Keith Richards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jagger-Richards.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1713" data-file-width="1915" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jagger-Richards.jpg/220px-Jagger-Richards.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jagger-Richards.jpg/330px-Jagger-Richards.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jagger-Richards.jpg/440px-Jagger-Richards.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jagger-Richards.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger and Richards sharing vocals at a concert in San Francisco during the Rolling Stones 1972 US tour</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jagger's relationship with band mate Richards is frequently described as "<a href="/wiki/Love%E2%80%93hate_relationship" title="Love–hate relationship">love/hate</a>" by the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Richards himself said in a 1998 interview: "I think of our differences as a family squabble. If I shout and scream at him, it's because no one else has the guts to do it or else they're paid not to do it. At the same time I'd hope Mick realises that I'm a friend who is just trying to bring him into line and do what needs to be done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Richards, along with <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>, tried unsuccessfully to persuade Jagger to appear in <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides</a></i>, alongside Depp and Richards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Richards' autobiography, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(book)" title="Life (book)">Life</a></i>, was released on 26 October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 October 2010, the Associated Press published an article stating that Richards refers to Jagger as "unbearable" in the book and notes that their relationship has been strained "for decades."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_and_film_production">Acting and film production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Acting and film production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Jagger has also had an intermittent acting career, most notably in <a href="/wiki/Donald_Cammell" title="Donald Cammell">Donald Cammell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Roeg" title="Nicolas Roeg">Nicolas Roeg</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Performance_(film)" title="Performance (film)">Performance</a></i> (1968) and as Australian <a href="/wiki/Bushranger" title="Bushranger">bushranger</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly_(1970_film)" title="Ned Kelly (1970 film)">Ned Kelly</a></i> (1970).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> He composed an improvised soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Anger" title="Kenneth Anger">Kenneth Anger</a>'s film <i>Invocation of My Demon Brother</i> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moog_synthesiser" title="Moog synthesiser">Moog synthesiser</a> in 1969. He auditioned for the role of Dr. Frank N. Furter in the 1975 film adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rocky_Horror_Picture_Show" title="The Rocky Horror Picture Show">The Rocky Horror Picture Show</a></i>, a role that was eventually played by the original performer from its run on London's West End, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Curry" title="Tim Curry">Tim Curry</a>. The same year, he was approached to play the role of <a href="/wiki/Feyd-Rautha" title="Feyd-Rautha">Feyd-Rautha</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> in the adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Frank_Herbert" title="Frank Herbert">Frank Herbert</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dune_(novel)" title="Dune (novel)">Dune</a> by director <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Jodorowsky" title="Alejandro Jodorowsky">Alejandro Jodorowsky</a> who approached Jagger by himself,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> but the movie never made it to the screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> He appeared as himself in <a href="/wiki/The_Rutles" title="The Rutles">the Rutles</a>' film <i><a href="/wiki/All_You_Need_Is_Cash" title="All You Need Is Cash">All You Need Is Cash</a></i> in 1978. In the late 1970s, Jagger was cast as Wilbur, a main character in <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">Werner Herzog</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Fitzcarraldo" title="Fitzcarraldo">Fitzcarraldo</a>.</i> However, a delay and the illness of main actor <a href="/wiki/Jason_Robards" title="Jason Robards">Jason Robards</a> (later replaced by <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Kinski" title="Klaus Kinski">Klaus Kinski</a>) in the film's notoriously difficult production resulted in his being unable to continue due to schedule conflicts with a band tour; some of the footage of his work are shown in the documentaries <i><a href="/wiki/Burden_of_Dreams" title="Burden of Dreams">Burden of Dreams</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/My_Best_Fiend" title="My Best Fiend">My Best Fiend</a></i>. In 1983, he starred in <a href="/wiki/Faerie_Tale_Theatre" title="Faerie Tale Theatre">Faerie Tale Theatre</a>'s <i>The Nightingale</i> as the emperor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> He developed a reputation for playing the heavy later in his acting career in films including <i><a href="/wiki/Freejack" title="Freejack">Freejack</a></i> (1992), <i><a href="/wiki/Bent_(film)" title="Bent (film)">Bent</a></i> (1997), and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Man_From_Elysian_Fields" title="The Man From Elysian Fields">The Man From Elysian Fields</a></i> (2002).</p>
<p>In 1995, Jagger founded Jagged Films with Victoria Pearman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Its first release was the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Enigma_(2001_film)" title="Enigma (2001 film)">Enigma</a></i> in 2001. That same year, it produced a documentary on Jagger entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Being_Mick" title="Being Mick">Being Mick</a>.</i> The programme, which first aired on television 22 November, coincided with the release of his fourth solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Goddess_in_the_Doorway" title="Goddess in the Doorway">Goddess in the Doorway</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, the company began work on <a href="/wiki/The_Women_(2008_film)" title="The Women (2008 film)"><i>The Women</i></a>, an adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/George_Cukor" title="George Cukor">George Cukor</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Women_(1939_film)" title="The Women (1939 film)">film of the same name</a>. It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Diane_English" title="Diane English">Diane English</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Rolling Stones have been the subjects of numerous documentaries, including <i><a href="/wiki/Gimme_Shelter_(1970_film)" title="Gimme Shelter (1970 film)">Gimme Shelter</a></i>, which was filmed during the band's 1969 tour of the US, and 1968's <a href="/wiki/Sympathy_for_the_Devil_(film)" title="Sympathy for the Devil (film)">Sympathy for the Devil</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/French_New_Wave" title="French New Wave">French New Wave</a> director <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Godard" title="Jean-Luc Godard">Jean-Luc Godard</a>. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> worked with Jagger on <i><a href="/wiki/Shine_a_Light_(film)" title="Shine a Light (film)">Shine a Light</a></i>, a documentary film featuring the Rolling Stones with footage from the A Bigger Bang Tour during two nights of performances at New York's Beacon Theatre. It screened in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in February 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a>'</i>s Todd McCarthy said the film "takes full advantage of heavy camera coverage and top-notch sound to create an invigorating musical trip down memory lane, as well as to provoke gentle musings on the wages of ageing and the passage of time." He predicted the film would fare better once released to video than in its limited theatrical runs. He was a co-producer of, and guest-starred in the first episode of the short-lived comedy American television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Knights_of_Prosperity" title="The Knights of Prosperity">The Knights of Prosperity</a></i>. He also co-produced the 2014 <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a> biopic, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Get_On_Up_(film)" title="Get On Up (film)">Get On Up</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:129px;max-width:129px">
<div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Spouses</div>
<div style="margin:1px;width:127px;max-width:127px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bianca_Jagger.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="367" data-file-width="286" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Bianca_Jagger.jpg/125px-Bianca_Jagger.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Bianca_Jagger.jpg/188px-Bianca_Jagger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Bianca_Jagger.jpg/250px-Bianca_Jagger.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Bianca_Jagger" title="Bianca Jagger">Bianca De Macias</a>, Jagger's first wife</div>
</div>
<div style="margin:1px;width:127px;max-width:127px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="439" data-file-width="344" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Jerry_Hall.jpg/125px-Jerry_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Jerry_Hall.jpg/188px-Jerry_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Jerry_Hall.jpg/250px-Jerry_Hall.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Model <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hall" title="Jerry Hall">Jerry Hall</a>, Jagger's second wife</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jagger has been married twice and has had several other relationships.</p>
<p>From 1966 to 1970, he had a relationship with <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Faithfull" title="Marianne Faithfull">Marianne Faithfull</a>, the singer/songwriter/actress with whom he wrote "<a href="/wiki/Sister_Morphine" title="Sister Morphine">Sister Morphine</a>", a song on the Rolling Stones' 1971 album <i><a href="/wiki/Sticky_Fingers" title="Sticky Fingers">Sticky Fingers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1970 he met <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaraguan</a>-born <a href="/wiki/Bianca_Jagger" title="Bianca Jagger">Bianca De Macias</a>. They married on 12 May 1971 in a Catholic ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Tropez" title="Saint-Tropez">Saint-Tropez</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. They separated in 1977, and in May 1978 she filed for divorce on the grounds of his adultery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Later she reportedly stated: "My marriage ended on my wedding day." In late 1977, Jagger began seeing model <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hall" title="Jerry Hall">Jerry Hall</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and they moved in together and had 4 children. They married in a Hindu beach ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> on 21 November 1990, and lived at <a href="/wiki/Downe_House,_Richmond_Hill" title="Downe House, Richmond Hill">Downe House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">Richmond, London</a>. Jagger contested the validity of the wedding ceremony, and the marriage was annulled in August 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger had a relationship with fashion designer <a href="/wiki/L%27Wren_Scott" title="L'Wren Scott">L'Wren Scott</a> from 2001 until her suicide in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> She left her entire estate, estimated at about <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US</a>$9 million, to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Children">Children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jagger has seven children with four women:</p>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>With <a href="/wiki/Marsha_Hunt_(singer_and_novelist)" title="Marsha Hunt (singer and novelist)">Marsha Hunt</a>, he has daughter Karis Hunt Jagger (born 4 November 1970).</li>
<li>With first wife <a href="/wiki/Bianca_Jagger" title="Bianca Jagger">Bianca Jagger</a>, he has daughter <a href="/wiki/Jade_Jagger" title="Jade Jagger">Jade Sheena Jezebel Jagger</a> (born 21 October 1971).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>With second wife <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hall" title="Jerry Hall">Jerry Hall</a>, he has daughter <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Jagger" title="Elizabeth Jagger">Elizabeth 'Lizzie' Scarlett Jagger</a> (born 2 March 1984), son James Leroy Augustin Jagger (born 28 August 1985), daughter <a href="/wiki/Georgia_May_Jagger" title="Georgia May Jagger">Georgia May Ayeesha Jagger</a> (born 12 January 1992), and son Gabriel Luke Beauregard Jagger (born 9 December 1997).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>With <a href="/wiki/Luciana_Gimenez" title="Luciana Gimenez">Luciana Gimenez</a>, he has a son, Lucas Maurice Morad Jagger (born 18 May 1999).</li>
</ul>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>He also has five grandchildren,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCOLImlucky_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCOLImlucky-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> and became a great-grandfather on 19 May 2014, when Jade's daughter Assisi gave birth to a daughter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hells_Angels">Hells Angels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hells Angels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Meredith_Hunter" title="Death of Meredith Hunter">Death of Meredith Hunter</a></div>
<p>In 2008, it was revealed that members of the <a href="/wiki/Hells_Angels" title="Hells Angels">Hells Angels</a> had plotted to murder Jagger in 1975. They were angered by Jagger's having publicly blamed the Angels, who had been hired to provide security at the <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Free_Concert" title="Altamont Free Concert">Altamont Free Concert</a> in December 1969, for much of the crowd violence at the event, in which Meredith Hunter, a black man, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Meredith_Hunter" title="Death of Meredith Hunter">was stabbed and beaten to death</a> by several Angels. Three other people also died at the event, attended by 350,000 people.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Hunter came running through the crowd, pursued by a biker who simply did not like the fact that Hunter's girlfriend was white ... Hunter - hard to miss in a green suit and large hat - pulled out a gun in a desperate act of self-defense... Hell's Angel Alan Passaro [was] the first to plunge a knife into Hunter" but found not guilty by a jury, purportedly because "so many of his fellow Angels were captured on film stabbing the young man [Hunter]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The conspirators reportedly used a boat to approach a residence where Jagger was staying on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_Island,_New_York" title="Long Island, New York">Long Island, New York</a>; the plot failed when the boat nearly sank in a storm and the plotters were forced to swim for their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Basil "Joe" Jagger, died of pneumonia on 11 November 2006 at age 93.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Although the Rolling Stones were on the A Bigger Bang Tour, Jagger flew to Britain on Friday to see his father before returning to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> the same day, where he was to perform on Saturday night. The show went ahead as scheduled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger is an avid <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> fan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> He founded <b>Jagged Internetworks</b> to cover English cricket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger is an avid supporter of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a> and has regularly attended <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> games, appearing at <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">France 98</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">Germany 2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">South Africa 2010</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">Brazil 2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2014, Jagger was one of 200 public figures who were signatories to a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> opposing <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a> in the run-up to September's <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">referendum on that issue</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> His personal fortune was estimated in 2010, at <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>190 million (~$298 million US).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Knighthood">Knighthood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Knighthood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2002_Birthday_Honours#Knights_Bachelor" title="2002 Birthday Honours">Queen's Birthday Honours 2002</a> Jagger was appointed a <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">Knight Bachelor</a> <i>for services to music</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> and on 12 December 2003 he was knighted by <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">HRH The Prince of Wales</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SirMick_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-SirMick-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Mick Jagger's knighthood received mixed reactions. Some fans were disappointed when he accepted the honour as it seemed to contradict his anti-establishment stance. As <a href="/wiki/United_Press_International" title="United Press International">UPI</a> noted in December 2003, Jagger has no "known record of charitable work or public services" although he is a patron of the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>. Jagger was on record as saying "apart from the Rolling Stones, the Queen is the best thing Britain has got", but was absent from the Queen's Golden Jubilee pop concert at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> that marked her 50 years on the throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Charlie Watts was quoted in the book <i>According to the Rolling Stones</i> as saying, "Anybody else would be lynched: 18 wives and 20 children and he's knighted, fantastic!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The ceremony took place in December 2003. Jagger’s father and daughters Karis and Elizabeth were in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger's knighthood also caused some friction between him and bandmate <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a>, who was irritated when Jagger accepted the "paltry honour".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Richards said that he did not want to take the stage with someone wearing a "coronet and sporting the old ermine. It's not what the Stones is about, is it?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SirMick_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-SirMick-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger retorted: "I think he would probably like to get the same honour himself. It's like being given an ice cream—one gets one and they all want one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SirMick_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-SirMick-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum,_Cleveland_(by_Adam_Jones).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg/180px-Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg/270px-Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg/360px-Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum%2C_Cleveland_%28by_Adam_Jones%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_1972_Tour_Jumpsuit_-_Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum,_Cleveland_(by_Adam_Jones).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger's jumpsuit from the Stones 1972 tour, on display at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> museum, Cleveland, Ohio</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the time that the Rolling Stones developed their anti-establishment image in the mid-1960s, Mick Jagger, with guitarist Keith Richards, has been an enduring icon of the counterculture. This was enhanced by his controversial drug-related arrests, sexually charged on-stage antics, provocative song lyrics, and his role of the bisexual Turner in the 1970 film <i><a href="/wiki/Performance_(film)" title="Performance (film)">Performance</a></i>. One of his biographers, Christopher Andersen, describes him as "one of the dominant cultural figures of our time", adding that Jagger was "the story of a generation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger, who at the time described himself as an <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> and espoused the leftist slogans of the era, took part in a demonstration against the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> outside the US Embassy in London in 1968. This event inspired him to write "<a href="/wiki/Street_Fighting_Man" title="Street Fighting Man">Street Fighting Man</a>" that same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> A variety of celebrities attended a lavish party at New York's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Regis_Hotel" title="St. Regis Hotel">St. Regis Hotel</a> to celebrate Jagger's 29th birthday and the end of the band's 1972 American tour. The party made the front pages of the leading New York newspapers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_(8717376688).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1000" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg/180px-Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg/270px-Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg/360px-Mick_Jagger_%288717376688%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick_Jagger_(8717376688).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger's military-style jacket worn during the 1989-1990 tour, on display at <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe" title="Hard Rock Cafe">Hard Rock Cafe</a>, Sydney, Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pop artist <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a> painted a series of silkscreen portraits of Jagger in 1975, one of which was owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farah_Diba" title="Farah Diba">Farah Diba</a>, wife of the <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Shah of Iran</a>. It hung on a wall inside the royal palace in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1967, <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Beaton" title="Cecil Beaton">Cecil Beaton</a> photographed Jagger's naked buttocks, a photo that sold at <a href="/wiki/Sotheby%27s" title="Sotheby's">Sotheby's</a> auction house in 1986 for $4,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Jagger was allegedly a contender for the anonymous subject of <a href="/wiki/Carly_Simon" title="Carly Simon">Carly Simon</a>'s 1973 hit song "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_So_Vain" title="You're So Vain">You're So Vain</a>", in which he sings backing vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Don_McLean" title="Don McLean">Don McLean</a> does not use Jagger's name in his famous song "<a href="/wiki/American_Pie_(song)" title="American Pie (song)">American Pie</a>", he alludes to Jagger onstage at <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Free_Concert" title="Altamont Free Concert">Altamont</a>, calling him <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, a retrospective exhibition of portraits of Mick Jagger was presented at the festival <a href="/wiki/Rencontres_d%27Arles" title="Rencontres d'Arles">Rencontres d'Arles</a>, in France. The catalogue of the exhibition is the first photo album of Mick Jagger and shows his evolution over 50 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> He was listed as one of the fifty best-dressed over 50s by the <i>Guardian</i> in March 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a>'s popular song "<a href="/wiki/Moves_like_Jagger" title="Moves like Jagger">Moves like Jagger</a>" is about Jagger. Jagger himself acknowledged the song in an interview, calling the concept "very flattering."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger is also referenced in <a href="/wiki/Kesha" title="Kesha">Kesha</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Tik_Tok" title="Tik Tok">Tik Tok</a>", <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">the Black Eyed Peas</a>' hit "<a href="/wiki/The_Time_(Dirty_Bit)" title="The Time (Dirty Bit)">The Time (Dirty Bit)</a>", and his vocal delivery is referenced by rapper <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> in the <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swagga_Like_Us" title="Swagga Like Us">Swagga Like Us</a>".</p>
<p>The 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/Almost_Famous" title="Almost Famous">Almost Famous</a></i>, set in 1974, refers to Jagger: "Because if you think Mick Jagger'll still be out there, trying to be a rock star at age 50... you're sadly, sadly mistaken."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg/240px-Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg/360px-Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg/480px-Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mick-Jagger_with_the_Rolling_Stones_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jagger singing during the Rolling Stones' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50_%26_Counting_Tour" title="50 &amp; Counting Tour">50 &amp; Counting Tour</a> in Boston, Massachusetts, 12 June 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the words of British dramatist and novelist <a href="/wiki/Philip_Norman_(author)" title="Philip Norman (author)">Philip Norman</a>, "the only point concerning Mick Jagger's influence over 'young people' that doctors and psychologists agreed on was that it wasn't, under any circumstances, fundamentally harmless."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norman_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-norman-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Norman, even <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> at his most scandalous had not exerted a "power so wholly and disturbingly physical": "Presley", he wrote in 1984, "while he made girls scream, did not have Jagger's ability to make men feel uncomfortable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norman_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-norman-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Norman also associates the early performances of Jagger with the Rolling Stones in the 1960s as a male ballet dancer, with "his conflicting and colliding sexuality: the swan's neck and smeared harlot eyes allied to an overstuffed and straining codpiece."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norman_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-norman-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Other authors also attribute similar connotations to Jagger. His performance style has been studied in the academic field as an analysis concerning gender, image and sexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> It has been written for example that his performance style "opened up definitions of gendered masculinity and so laid the foundations for self-invention and sexual plasticity which are now an integral part of contemporary <a href="/wiki/Youth_culture" title="Youth culture">youth culture</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheila_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheila-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> His stage personas also contributed significantly to the British tradition of popular music that always featured the character song and where the art of singing becomes a matter of acting—which creates a question concerning the singer's relationship to his own words.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> His voice has been described as a powerful expressive tool for communicating feelings to his audience and expressing an alternative vision of society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australasianjornal_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-australasianjornal-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> To express "virility and unrestrained passion" he developed techniques previously used by African American preachers and <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> singers such as "the roar, the guttural belt style of singing, and the buzz, a more nasal and raspy sound".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australasianjornal_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-australasianjornal-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steven_Van_Zandt" title="Steven Van Zandt">Steven Van Zandt</a> also wrote: "The acceptance of Jagger's voice on pop radio was a turning point in rock &amp; roll. He broke open the door for everyone else. Suddenly, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Burdon" title="Eric Burdon">Eric Burdon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Van_Morrison" title="Van Morrison">Van Morrison</a> weren't so weird – even <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> has described Jagger as "one of the most popular and influential frontmen in the history of rock &amp; roll".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Musician <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> joined many rock bands with blues, folk and soul orientations in his first attempts as a musician in the mid-1960s, and he was to recall: "I used to dream of being their Mick Jagger".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Bowie would also offer that "I think Mick Jagger would be astounded and amazed if he realized that to many people he is not a <a href="/wiki/Sex_symbol" title="Sex symbol">sex symbol</a>, but a mother image."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Jagger appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> '​s List of 100 Greatest Singers at number 16; in the article, <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz" title="Lenny Kravitz">Lenny Kravitz</a> wrote: "I sometimes talk to people who sing perfectly in a technical sense who don't understand Mick Jagger. [...] His sense of pitch and melody is really sophisticated. His vocals are stunning, flawless in their own kind of perfection."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstoneslist_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstoneslist-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> This edition also cites Mick Jagger as a key influence on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jack_White_(musician)" title="Jack White (musician)">Jack White</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Tyler" title="Steven Tyler">Steven Tyler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iggy_Pop" title="Iggy Pop">Iggy Pop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstoneslist_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstoneslist-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>More recently, his cultural legacy is also associated with his ageing accompanied by some vitality. <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Jon_Bon_Jovi" title="Jon Bon Jovi">Jon Bon Jovi</a>, also a veteran, has said: "We continue to make Number One records and fill stadiums. But will we still be doing 150 shows per tour? I just can't see it. I don't know how the hell Mick Jagger does it at 67. That would be the first question I'd ask him. He runs around the stage as much as I do yet he's got almost 20 years on me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Since his early career, Jagger embodied what some authors describes as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dionysian" title="Dionysian">Dionysian</a> <a href="/wiki/Archetype" title="Archetype">archetype</a>" of "eternal youth" personified by many rock stars and the rock culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> As wrote biographer Laura Jackson, "It is impossible to imagine current culture without the unique influence of Mick Jagger."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_albums">Solo albums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mick_Jagger&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Solo albums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">

<th><small><a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">US</a></small></th>

<tr>
<td>1985</td>
<td><i><b><a href="/wiki/She%27s_the_Boss" title="She's the Boss">She's the Boss</a></b></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: 21 February 1985</li>
